## Recap
​
In the last post, I covered how to get set up with [SQLCell](https://github.com/tmthyjames/SQLCell) and explored the basic features. If you missed it, be sure to check it out [here](https://tmthyjames.github.io/projects/SQLCell-Part-I/). 
​
To summarize, I went over <br/>
​
1) the installation process<br/>
​
2) what each of the buttons do<br/>
​
3) how to declare multiple engines<br/>
​
4) passing variables back and forth between Python and SQL<br/>
​
5) the query plan table and the d3.js sankey optimization plan graph<br/><br/>
​
​
​
This time, we'll go deeper and see what else it can do.

Recap¶

In the last post, I covered how to get set up with SQLCell and explored the basic features. If you missed it, be sure to check it out here.

To summarize, I went over

1) the installation process

2) what each of the buttons do

3) how to declare multiple engines

4) passing variables back and forth between Python and SQL

5) the query plan table and the d3.js sankey optimization plan graph

This time, we'll go deeper and see what else it can do.

## Flags
​
In [the last post](https://tmthyjames.github.io/projects/SQLCell-Part-I/) we [covered](https://tmthyjames.github.io/projects/SQLCell-Part-I/#Declaring Engines) one flag function, `--declare_engines`. This time we'll explore the `--pg_dump` flag. If you use PostgreSQL then this functionality will look familiar. It let's you run `pg_dump` commands from the kernel.
<br/><br/>
For instance, if you wanted to dump a table to a file then you could do the following code. This database is a great resource for NBA data and can be found [here](https://github.com/tmthyjames/SQLCell/blob/master/data/sports.sql).

Flags¶

In the last post we covered one flag function, --declare_engines. This time we'll explore the --pg_dump flag. If you use PostgreSQL then this functionality will look familiar. It let's you run pg_dump commands from the kernel.

For instance, if you wanted to dump a table to a file then you could do the following code. This database is a great resource for NBA data and can be found here.

In [4]:
%%sql --pg_dump
-t nba sports
--
-- PostgreSQL database dump
--

-- Dumped from database version 9.6.2
-- Dumped by pg_dump version 9.6.2

SET statement_timeout = 0;
SET lock_timeout = 0;
SET idle_in_transaction_session_timeout = 0;
SET client_encoding = 'UTF8';
SET standard_conforming_strings = on;
SET check_function_bodies = false;
SET client_min_messages = warning;
SET row_security = off;

SET search_path = public, pg_catalog;

SET default_tablespace = '';

SET default_with_oids = false;

--
-- Name: nba; Type: TABLE; Schema: public; Owner: postgres
--

CREATE TABLE nba (
    dateof date,
    team character varying(5),
    opp character varying(5),
    pts bigint,
    fg integer,
    fg_att integer,
    ft integer,
    ft_att integer,
    fg3 integer,
    fg3_att integer,
    off_rebounds integer,
    def_rebounds integer,
    asst integer,
    blks integer,
    fouls integer,
    stls integer,
    turnovers integer
);


ALTER TABLE nba OWNER TO postgres;

--
-- Data for Name: nba; Type: TABLE DATA; Schema: public; Owner: postgres
--

COPY nba (dateof, team, opp, pts, fg, fg_att, ft, ft_att, fg3, fg3_att, off_rebounds, def_rebounds, asst, blks, fouls, stls, turnovers) FROM stdin;

## Inline Value Editing
​
This feature allows the user to edit a value directly from the output, assuming the table has a primary key and is not produced by a join. To edit the values just set the `EDIT` parameter to `True`. First, we'll query the rows with the most shares, then we'll rename some of the values in the network and article columns

Inline Value Editing¶

This feature allows the user to edit a value directly from the output, assuming the table has a primary key and is not produced by a join. To edit the values just set the EDIT parameter to True. First, we'll query the rows with the most shares, then we'll rename some of the values in the network and article columns

In [6]:
%%sql DB=sidekick EDIT=True
select * from shares order by shares desc limit 5

To execute: 0.01 sec | Rows: 5 | DB: sidekick | Host: localhost | EDIT MODE

## Inline Column Modification
​
We'll use the same parameter, `EDIT`, and the `psql` meta-command `\d` to change the column types and names. Here are our original values.

Inline Column Modification¶

We'll use the same parameter, EDIT, and the psql meta-command \d to change the column types and names. Here are our original values.

## Transaction Blocks
​
Some SQL commands cannot be run inside of a transaction block. For instance, `CREATE`ing or `DROP`ing a database, or `VACUUM ANALYZE`ing a database are statements that must be run outside of a transaction block. Using the `TRANSACTION_BLOCK` parameter, we can accomplish this. First, let's try to `CREATE` a database inside a transaction block.

Transaction Blocks¶

Some SQL commands cannot be run inside of a transaction block. For instance, CREATEing or DROPing a database, or VACUUM ANALYZEing a database are statements that must be run outside of a transaction block. Using the TRANSACTION_BLOCK parameter, we can accomplish this. First, let's try to CREATE a database inside a transaction block.

In [3]:
%%sql
CREATE DATABASE dummy;
Exception in thread Thread-8:
Traceback (most recent call last):
  File "/Users/tdobbins/anaconda/lib/python2.7/threading.py", line 801, in __bootstrap_inner
    self.run()
  File "/Users/tdobbins/anaconda/lib/python2.7/threading.py", line 754, in run
    self.__target(*self.__args, **self.__kwargs)
  File "/Users/tdobbins/.ipython/profile_default/startup/SQLCell/sqlcell.py", line 184, in _SQL
    data = connection.execute(cell, reduce(functools.partial(build_dict, __KERNEL_VARS__=__KERNEL_VARS__), matches, {}))
  File "/Users/tdobbins/anaconda/lib/python2.7/site-packages/sqlalchemy/engine/base.py", line 939, in execute
    return self._execute_text(object, multiparams, params)
  File "/Users/tdobbins/anaconda/lib/python2.7/site-packages/sqlalchemy/engine/base.py", line 1097, in _execute_text
    statement, parameters
  File "/Users/tdobbins/anaconda/lib/python2.7/site-packages/sqlalchemy/engine/base.py", line 1189, in _execute_context
    context)
  File "/Users/tdobbins/anaconda/lib/python2.7/site-packages/sqlalchemy/engine/base.py", line 1393, in _handle_dbapi_exception
    exc_info
  File "/Users/tdobbins/anaconda/lib/python2.7/site-packages/sqlalchemy/util/compat.py", line 203, in raise_from_cause
    reraise(type(exception), exception, tb=exc_tb, cause=cause)
  File "/Users/tdobbins/anaconda/lib/python2.7/site-packages/sqlalchemy/engine/base.py", line 1182, in _execute_context
    context)
  File "/Users/tdobbins/anaconda/lib/python2.7/site-packages/sqlalchemy/engine/default.py", line 470, in do_execute
    cursor.execute(statement, parameters)
InternalError: (psycopg2.InternalError) CREATE DATABASE cannot run inside a transaction block
 [SQL: 'CREATE DATABASE dummy;']
. . .
xxxxxxxxxx
Notice we get an `InternalError` about the transaction block. We just need to set the `TRANSACTION_BLOCK` parameter to `False`.

Notice we get an InternalError about the transaction block. We just need to set the TRANSACTION_BLOCK parameter to False.

In [6]:
%%sql TRANSACTION_BLOCK=False
CREATE DATABASE dummy;

Query finished... | To execute: 0.36 sec | DB: sports | Host: localhost

. . .
xxxxxxxxxx

## What Next?
​
My main focus at this point is knocking out the [issues](https://github.com/tmthyjames/SQLCell/issues) and optimizing SQLCell for all major relational databases. Please don't hesitate to submit some pull requests. Enjoy!

What Next?¶

My main focus at this point is knocking out the issues and optimizing SQLCell for all major relational databases. Please don't hesitate to submit some pull requests. Enjoy!
